<script>
  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_41eb76eb-6eda-4895-9f35-5b17a0025779'
      });
    }
    
    var initializeSiwa = function() {
      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"
      loadScript(APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL, initAppleId);
    };
    if (typeof AppleID !== "undefined") {
      initAppleId();
    } else {
      initializeSiwa();
    }

</script>

If winning Tim’s heart was an impossible quest, keeping it would prove even harder as family, society, and emotion threaten to tear them apart.<br /><br /><em>Something Like Summer</em> is a love story spanning a decade and beyond as two boys discover what it means to be friends, lovers, and sometimes even enemies.</span>

        }
      });

      newTip['wrapper'].addClassName('prototipAllowOverflow');

        $('edition_10187586').observe('prototip:shown', function () {
          $$('div.prototip').each(function (e) {
            if ($('edition_10187586').hasClassName('ignored')) {
              e.setStyle({'display': 'none'});
              return;

            e.setStyle({'overflow': 'visible'});
          });

    <a title="Susan" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/739211-susan"><img alt="Susan" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1335133091p2/739211.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/415556623?book_show_action=true">Sep 16, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Susan" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Susan" href="/user/show/739211-susan">Susan</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer415556623" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13547371741584332071"><br/>2.5 Stars.<br/><br/>Here. <i>*hands over GR membership card*</i> <br/><br/>It’s at this point that it’s clear <b>I’M</b> the issue. Everyone LOVED this book. Me? I’m just barely above strongly disliking it. <br/><br/><u>I’ll try to do this without any major spoilers:</u><br/><br/>* I didn’t find teenaged Ben or Tim to be that likeable or charming. <br/>* The entire “Part 2” portion was slow and boring.<br/>* I hate love triangles.<br/>* Adult Tim is creepy, overbearing, desperate, borderline pathetic and a stalker.<br/>* Adult Ben is irresponsible, overly emotional, inapprop</span>
  <span id="freeText13547371741584332071" style="display:none"><br />2.5 Stars.<br /><br />Here. <i>*hands over GR membership card*</i> <br /><br />It’s at this point that it’s clear <b>I’M</b> the issue. Everyone LOVED this book. Me? I’m just barely above strongly disliking it. <br /><br /><u>I’ll try to do this without any major spoilers:</u><br /><br />* I didn’t find teenaged Ben or Tim to be that likeable or charming. <br />* The entire “Part 2” portion was slow and boring.<br />* I hate love triangles.<br />* Adult Tim is creepy, overbearing, desperate, borderline pathetic and a stalker.<br />* Adult Ben is irresponsible, overly emotional, inappropriate, and unfaithful.	<br />* Jace is perfect. <br />* The writing was ok, but the storyline ALL over the place.<br />* And, and…I will be annoying and say…I TOTALLY CALLED THAT ENDING…for some reason, I just knew that’s what was going to happen exactly as the last few chapters played out…<br /><br />The fact that I didn’t shed a tear when so many of my GR friends were, as they put it, a “weeping mess”…well, if ever I questioned being cold &amp; dead inside, this might prove it true…not a tear dropped…but maybe some f-bombs dropped in frustration.<br /><br />But don’t listen to me…I’m alone on an island…(and PS – I probably WILL read “Something Like Winter”…because I’m curious…and I just like to torture myself…)<br /><br /></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer475754742" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7003884400253308189"><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1472750173i/20237706._SX540_.jpg' width='200' height='150' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>*1.5 stars* <br/><br/><b>HOLY CRAP. This book exhausted me in every way. </b><br/><br/>This isn't going to be a <i>review</i>, review. I'm simply just going to blurt out some thoughts. Some will be spoiler-tagged. <i>*Help me organize my thoughts, Beyoncé*</i><br/><br/><b>Tim is an obsessed, narcissistic stalker.</b> All of that stuff he did to Ben and Jace in Ben's college years. <i>*fumes*</i> I see some of my fellow readers loving Tim, but I can't even COUNT the number of times I've bitch-slapped him in my head. His face is all red and ugly looking right n</span>
  <span id="freeText7003884400253308189" style="display:none"><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1472750173i/20237706._SX540_.jpg" width="200" height="150" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>*1.5 stars* <br><br><b>HOLY CRAP. This book exhausted me in every way. </b><br><br>This isn't going to be a <i>review</i>, review. I'm simply just going to blurt out some thoughts. Some will be spoiler-tagged. <i>*Help me organize my thoughts, Beyoncé*</i><br><br><b>Tim is an obsessed, narcissistic stalker.</b> All of that stuff he did to Ben and Jace in Ben's college years. <i>*fumes*</i> I see some of my fellow readers loving Tim, but I can't even COUNT the number of times I've bitch-slapped him in my head. His face is all red and ugly looking right now. <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1467055035ra/19546825.gif" width="370" height="200" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><b>Jace is a doormat who is too perfect.</b> That's right, I said it. He is TOO PERFECT. If my man <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[cheated on me <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> I would do soooo much more than just <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[shrug and say that everything was okay and that I understand. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> He treated Ben like a freakin' prince and all he got in return was to be <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[killed off in the end like an inconvenience. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> I wanted Jace to ditch them ALL, and run off in to sunset with someone else. <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1467056215ra/19547037.gif" width="370" height="200" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><b>Ben is a <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[cheating <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>, dramatic, brat.</b> I actually hated Ben in his high school years. I kept thinking what a total dick he was to his family and teachers at school, though, granted, most teenagers are dicks. I felt for him a little bit, but I really disliked his "me, me, me" attitude. When Ben was older, I didn't grow to like him more. I sort of tolerated him, but he didn't grow on me. Also, don't forgive him for how he treated Jace. I just don't!<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1467056054ra/19547013.gif" width="370" height="200" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>The writing was... good, I guess, but I thought that this book felt like a few different books smushed into one. I get that it was supposed to be an epic love story through the ages, but I just didn't really enjoy the different time periods put together into one book. <br><br>I also just HATE <b>love triangles</b>. Like, I really hate them. It stressed me out to read about them, and I don't want to read about <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[CHEATERS <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>. I'm getting <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/669790.The_Hell_You_Say__The_Adrien_English_Mysteries___3_" title="The Hell You Say (The Adrien English Mysteries, #3) by Josh Lanyon" rel="nofollow noopener">The Hell You Say</a> flashbacks over here. <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1467057172ra/19547192.gif" width="370" height="200" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><b>The audiobook narration was... okay.</b> Nothing special, if I'm being honest. It was decent, but sometimes a great narrator can turn a book that I sort of hate into one that I really enjoy (see <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/669790.The_Hell_You_Say__The_Adrien_English_Mysteries___3_" title="The Hell You Say (The Adrien English Mysteries, #3) by Josh Lanyon" rel="nofollow noopener">The Hell You Say</a> and my review for it <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/914727754?book_show_action=false">https://www.goodreads.com/review/show...</a>). The narration was worth the $1.99 that I paid for it, for sure, but it wasn't fabulous. <br><br>And while everyone else was sobbing at the ending, I was just MAD how it all went down. Like furious. I was screaming, "DO SOMETHING," at Ben, probably out loud. It felt so pointless. And I just knew that something like that would happen!!<br> <br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1467057172ra/19547193.gif" width="370" height="200" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>After listening to the audio book for about <b>10 hours</b>, I'm just TIRED. I need an emotional break. <br><br>I'm out, y'all.</["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></span>
  <a data-text-id="7003884400253308189" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/39893246-nazanin?shelf=m-m">m-m</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
                  <em>
                    This review has been hidden because it contains spoilers. To view it,
                    <a href="#" onclick="Effect.toggle(&#39;reviewTextContainer3522583863&#39;); return false;">click here.</a>

              <span id="reviewTextContainer3522583863" class="readable"
                    style="display:none"

<span id="freeTextContainer2412642725110490835"><b>5 Stars</b><br/><br/><i>Teach me how to fly,<br/>my beautiful butterfly.</i><br/><br/>And that’s what Ben did. He taught Tim how to fly but so much happened in between. Some good, some bad, some painful, some confusing, some frustrating, some bitter, some sweet, and some just awesome… I’m sure most of you guys probably hated Tim for what he did or at some point did not but I loved him as much as Tim and Jace. I couldn’t just stop loving him. I loved Jace too, I couldn’t choose between them so I think the way the author managed to </span>
  <span id="freeText2412642725110490835" style="display:none"><b>5 Stars</b><br /><br /><i>Teach me how to fly,<br />my beautiful butterfly.</i><br /><br />And that’s what Ben did. He taught Tim how to fly but so much happened in between. Some good, some bad, some painful, some confusing, some frustrating, some bitter, some sweet, and some just awesome… I’m sure most of you guys probably hated Tim for what he did or at some point did not but I loved him as much as Tim and Jace. I couldn’t just stop loving him. I loved Jace too, I couldn’t choose between them so I think the way the author managed to finish the story was the best way (to me) and still I didn’t like it. I don’t like this kind of bittersweet endings that leave me feeling raw. And yet again I couldn’t think of any other ending. This story contains cheating and I didn’t mind, like at all!<br /><br />Told in single POV, 3rd person, it’s the first installment in the "Something Like" series and it can be read as a standalone. I checked other books in the series, book 2 is Jace’s story (I will skip it, because, well as I know what happened to him I don’t think my heart could bear it for the second time), and book 3 is Tim’s story. So book 3, it is! My first read by this author and loved it, hope you enjoy it as well!<br /><br /><i>Something Like Summer is a love story spanning a decade and beyond as two boys discover what it means to be friends, lovers, and sometimes even enemies. </i></span>

<div id="review_288587646" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/288587646" />
    <a title="Isa K." class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4471028-isa-k"><img alt="Isa K." src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/u_50x66-632230dc9882b4352d753eedf9396530.png" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/288587646?book_show_action=true">Mar 04, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Isa K." class="user" itemprop="url" name="Isa K." href="/user/show/4471028-isa-k">Isa K.</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4471028-isa-k?shelf=romance">romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4471028-isa-k?shelf=reading-challenge">reading-challenge</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer288587646" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12152533179040009199">Meh~<br/><br/>Just meh~ This book is basically two books sold as one. Part 1 on its own would have gotten 3 stars from me. It was okay, kind of uninspiring YA, but it steered away from all the melodrama I was expecting. That counts for something.<br/><br/>I'm a strong believer in judging YA-themed stories by the adult characters. Our cast in Something Like Summer includes many of the usual cliches: Rich Neglectful Parents, Abusive Controlling Tyrants, People So Liberal in Child Rearing It Borders on Criminal (other</span>
  <span id="freeText12152533179040009199" style="display:none">Meh~<br /><br />Just meh~ This book is basically two books sold as one. Part 1 on its own would have gotten 3 stars from me. It was okay, kind of uninspiring YA, but it steered away from all the melodrama I was expecting. That counts for something.<br /><br />I'm a strong believer in judging YA-themed stories by the adult characters. Our cast in Something Like Summer includes many of the usual cliches: Rich Neglectful Parents, Abusive Controlling Tyrants, People So Liberal in Child Rearing It Borders on Criminal (otherwise known as the 'cool parents' who seem okay with treating their kids like inconvenient social equals after a pretentious lecture from a self-righteous teenager) ... all we're missing is the Hip Teacher dishing out sagely life advice.<br /><br />In fairness, there are some attempts to move beyond these stereotypes and make the archetypes richer and more complex ... but not much. Ultimately this is a m/m love story.<br /><br />And about that love story. It grew on me. Tim is kind of an ass, but you see enough of his good side to tolerate it. Ben, is kind of pathetic ... but pathetic in the way teenagers in love typically are.<br /><br />So again, not over the moon, but there was enough sweetness to help me enjoy the trials and tribulations of Tim/Ben<br /><br />Then Part 2 came.<br /><br />Part 2 was a train wreck, an absolute train wreck in which all the likable characters from the first part might as well have been eaten by zombies. The characters we were supposed to rally around were bland and undeveloped. There was nary a rational thought in sight.<br /><br />Take for example Ben's best friend Allison. Part 2 starts with a three year jump. Everyone has gone away to college, Ben has moved across the country. He returns home <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[because Allison's father has died <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> and a distraught Allison begs him to transfer to her college for moral support. Apparently in three years, vivacious outgoing Allison <strong>
  <em>has made no friends???</em>
</strong> None at all? She needs to force her former bestie to uproot his entire life midsemester because in three years she hasn't grown close to anyone else?<br /><br />This seems inconsistant with the Allison we met in the beginning. A character who reached beyond the girl-wingman/cheap-therapist/author-avatar cliche we see so often in these books. She had her own life, her own issues, her own love interests in Part 1. In Part 2 her whole purpose is to direct the course of Ben's love life. Make sure he stays on the path to true luv.<br /><br />Bullshit.<br /><br />Tim meanwhile has gone from being a sweet, good natured guy whose sexual confusion causes him to act like an asshole from time to time ... to a desperate manipulative cock slut. *sigh* I'm so tired of controlling and abusive behavior being sold to people as a man showing the "vulnerability" and the intensity of his love. Bullshit Bullshit Bullshit.<br /><br />I don't even understand the point of Part 2. It seems to be devoted to giving Ben another love interest, but the author never really invests anything in Jace as a character. What color is his hair? His eyes? What (besides fortune cookies) are his interests? If it was there I certainly can't remember it. Jace is completely one-dimensional, bland in every conceivable way: he's always good, always faithful, always loves unconditional. We spend a lot of time with Ben/Jace but it ends up feeling like a romance <em>en summary</em>. There's no real emotion in their courtship because the author never wants you to want to see them together.<br /><br /><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[And when Jace dies tragically so that the door is open for Tim/Ben ... well by that time you've probably lost any interest in both Ben and Tim as characters that you can't even get annoyed at the final cliche f-u. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span></span>
  <a data-text-id="12152533179040009199" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_558491182" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/558491182" />
    <a title="Breann" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5378471-breann"><img alt="Breann" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1516391780p2/5378471.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/558491182?book_show_action=true">Mar 11, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Breann" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Breann" href="/user/show/5378471-breann">Breann</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

      <a href="/user/show/7234093-barb-rede-2-read">Barb ~rede-2-read~</a>

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5378471-breann?shelf=on-calibre">on-calibre</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5378471-breann?shelf=contemporary-romance">contemporary-romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5378471-breann?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5378471-breann?shelf=2014-rrrc-challenge">2014-rrrc-challenge</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5378471-breann?shelf=first-in-series">first-in-series</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5378471-breann?shelf=2013-rrrc-challenge">2013-rrrc-challenge</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5378471-breann?shelf=mm">mm</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5378471-breann?shelf=made-me-cry">made-me-cry</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5378471-breann?shelf=oh-the-angst">oh-the-angst</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5378471-breann?shelf=new-adult-college">new-adult-college</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer558491182" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14539243510598616365"><b>***Audio edition re-read***</b><br/><br/>Just as good as the first time. <br/><br/>Ben and his two great loves. Neither is better than the other and neither is stronger than the other. Just different. Different, but equally perfect and fitting for Ben.<br/><br/>__________________________________________<br/><br/>This is a review for both <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/10213367.Something_Like_Summer__Seasons___1_' title='Something Like Summer (Seasons, #1) by Jay Bell' rel='nofollow noopener'>Something Like Summer</a> and <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/16093007.Something_Like_Winter__Seasons___2_' title='Something Like Winter (Seasons, #2) by Jay Bell' rel='nofollow noopener'>Something Like Winter</a> since I don't see a way to talk about one without the other.<br/><br/><b>
  <i>“Why couldn't people's insides match their outsides? The world would be such a wonderful plac</i></b></span>
  <span id="freeText14539243510598616365" style="display:none"><b>***Audio edition re-read***</b><br /><br />Just as good as the first time. <br /><br />Ben and his two great loves. Neither is better than the other and neither is stronger than the other. Just different. Different, but equally perfect and fitting for Ben.<br /><br />__________________________________________<br /><br />This is a review for both <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/10213367.Something_Like_Summer__Seasons___1_" title="Something Like Summer (Seasons, #1) by Jay Bell" rel="nofollow noopener">Something Like Summer</a> and <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/16093007.Something_Like_Winter__Seasons___2_" title="Something Like Winter (Seasons, #2) by Jay Bell" rel="nofollow noopener">Something Like Winter</a> since I don't see a way to talk about one without the other.<br /><br /><b>
  <i>“Why couldn't people's insides match their outsides? The world would be such a wonderful place if the nicer someone was, the more beautiful they became.”</i>
</b><br /><br />I really don’t know where to begin with this review. Both books have left me with such high emotions that I’m still sitting here quite speechless. I can tell you this, when I started I was expecting a cute little coming of age tale. Ha! Yeah right. What I got was beautiful, heartbreaking, wonderfully written story that left me a blubbering mess. One that is on my mind and will continue to be on my mind for days. <br /><br />In the beginning of both books we meet Ben, an out and proud teenager, and Tim, a boy who is still trying to figure himself out and how he fits in the world. When they meet they start up a secret relationship because Tim, having to worry about his social status, can’t very much be seen with the local gay kid. Yeah, whatever Tim. The boys become closer and their relationship turns into a sexual one which then leads Ben to wanting exclusivity with Tim. Tim is still young and still scared. Scared of his own feelings, of his parents’ feelings, hell, he’s basically scared of the world. So he ran. <br /><br />In <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/10213367.Something_Like_Summer__Seasons___1_" title="Something Like Summer (Seasons, #1) by Jay Bell" rel="nofollow noopener">Something Like Summer</a> we have the story told through Ben’s POV. Ben had just been left by his first love and is in pieces. <u>Pieces</u>. With me right along with him. He is forced to move on and move on he does. He has a few boyfriends but he eventually finds love again with the ever-perfect, Jace. I <i>loved</i> Ben &amp; Jace’s story. Even though Ben never stopped loving Tim and he is still a very real presence in Ben’s life, Ben &amp; Jace’s relationship felt just as real and was wonderful to witness. Jace was everything Ben needed and deserved after his massive heartbreak. Jace was understanding, forgiving, loving and just completely there for him. Like I said, perfect. <br /><br />In <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/16093007.Something_Like_Winter__Seasons___2_" title="Something Like Winter (Seasons, #2) by Jay Bell" rel="nofollow noopener">Something Like Winter</a> the same story is told through Tim’s POV, but it didn’t feel as though I read the same story twice. They first 20% or so was Tim &amp; Ben’s relationship they had in high school and it was interesting to read what happened in Tim’s eyes. Let’s face it, it was going to take a lot to redeem some of Tim’s actions. Yes, Tim was redeemed but no, his actions were not excused. Not only did Tim break Ben’s heart but he tore his own into pieces by running. Right along with my heart. After he realizes his mistake, it’s too late. Ben has found someone he loves and deserves, Jace. Tim thought his life was over after Ben and struggles to get it back. He floats through life; he finds some successful relationships and some very damaging relationships along the way. His story was the most heartbreaking for me, he was so broken and so lost. Nobody to really love him except his best friend, Eric, but I <i>really</i> can’t go there right now. Still too many emotions running wild! But, eventually, he was able to put the pieces of his life back together. Not for Ben but because of Ben and the love they still had.<br /><br />Throughout the 10 year or so span of these books Ben &amp; Tim touch each others lives, coming in and out for brief moments but they were never able to find the right moment to be together. Well, in the end they finally found their moment. And it was beautiful.<br /><br />Oh my, this was so emotionally intense I cried like a little baby in both SLS and SLW. I don’t think I’ve cried like that while reading since Dobby died. You know what I mean. Yeah, that kind of cry. I was happy, sad, devastated, heartbroken, hopeful, just every emotion hit me, BAM! over and over again. Next up is <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/17975600.Something_Like_Autumn__Seasons___3_" title="Something Like Autumn (Seasons, #3) by Jay Bell" rel="nofollow noopener">Something Like Autumn</a> where we get to read Jace’s story. It’s ready to go on the Kindle but I still need some time to mend my heart before picking this story back up.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="14539243510598616365" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>


      <div class="reviewFooter uitext buttons">

<div id="review_293064492" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/293064492" />
    <a title="June Helmsley" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/8164744-june-helmsley"><img alt="June Helmsley" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1335292227p2/8164744.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/293064492?book_show_action=true">Mar 12, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="June Helmsley" class="user" itemprop="url" name="June Helmsley" href="/user/show/8164744-june-helmsley">June Helmsley</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8164744-june-helmsley?shelf=oh-hell-fucking-yes">oh-hell-fucking-yes</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8164744-june-helmsley?shelf=dudes-doing-dudes">dudes-doing-dudes</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer293064492" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer465036567082884471">Holy Fucking Shit!<br/><br/>That's what this book should be retitled, or maybe that can be the subtitle. I don't know, I'll get back to you on that. Either way, it needs a lot of exclamation points because Holy FuckSandwich does this book kick so much ass.<br/><br/>When reading fiction, it bothers me when I don't care about the characters, or even worse, a goddamn contrived love triangle that bores me when it should interest me. Not here! I was so emotionally invested in these characters that I lost my shit when ba</span>
  <span id="freeText465036567082884471" style="display:none">Holy Fucking Shit!<br /><br />That's what this book should be retitled, or maybe that can be the subtitle. I don't know, I'll get back to you on that. Either way, it needs a lot of exclamation points because Holy FuckSandwich does this book kick so much ass.<br /><br />When reading fiction, it bothers me when I don't care about the characters, or even worse, a goddamn contrived love triangle that bores me when it should interest me. Not here! I was so emotionally invested in these characters that I lost my shit when bad things happened to them. Seriously, I cried. Twice. And I never cry. When I told my roommate Amy Kennedy about that, she started accusing me of being human and having feelings and shit but after SHE read this book she was all kinds of touched by it too. So who's the human now, bitch?!!?<br /><br />Here's a gist: Ben is obsessed with Tim. Tim and Ben start a careful romance, but Tim's not out yet and he's kind of a jerk but you feel for him so it's sort of okay. The years go on and they go their seperate ways, and Ben meets up with this awesome guy named Jace and everything seems okay but then Holy Fuckdoodles Tim is back! Normally I despise love triangles but in this it feels so real! <br /><br />It kinda reminded me of the Luke and Noah and Reid thing on As the World Turns, which I never would have fucking watched but then I caught clips on YouTube and got addicted and stayed up one whole weekend watching it. I lost my shit with those guys and thanks to SLS I lost it again!<br /><br />What's nice about this book is that everything that happens to these characters feels believable, and you can empathize with them and the decisions they make. Also, no vampires, and these days, that's a plus.<br /><br />I know I'm rambling, but I think Amy mixed up my pills or put an extra shot of B12 in my smoothie this morning because I'm screaming at the screen as I type this! READ! THIS! FUCKING! BOOK!<br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="465036567082884471" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_952912177" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/952912177" />
    <a title="Vivian" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3947172-vivian"><img alt="Vivian" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1458107851p2/3947172.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/952912177?book_show_action=true">May 30, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Vivian" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Vivian" href="/user/show/3947172-vivian">Vivian</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3947172-vivian?shelf=own">own</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3947172-vivian?shelf=ya-na">ya-na</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3947172-vivian?shelf=catharsis">catharsis</a>
          </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer952912177" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11113041529441378028">This... THIS is why I'd never want to relive my teenage years.<br/><br/>All that doubt, wondering, alienation---Ugh. Ben is a great narrator. At times, you want to cringe and others cheer, but like life, it has its ups and downs. To know something about yourself at a young age that makes you significantly different is an experience that isolates. Growth is different, changed and lonely. <br/><br/>Ben's early teen years came with a harsh lesson. Not all epiphanies lead to happiness. But like a good sword, it gets st</span>
  <span id="freeText11113041529441378028" style="display:none">This... THIS is why I'd never want to relive my teenage years.<br /><br />All that doubt, wondering, alienation---Ugh. Ben is a great narrator. At times, you want to cringe and others cheer, but like life, it has its ups and downs. To know something about yourself at a young age that makes you significantly different is an experience that isolates. Growth is different, changed and lonely. <br /><br />Ben's early teen years came with a harsh lesson. Not all epiphanies lead to happiness. But like a good sword, it gets stronger with each fold and hammer blow. Ben doesn't falter. His resilience is admirable and he's so far ahead of others in his personal growth that he has no confidant to share his hopes, dreams and desires--except for his best friend, Allison. <br /><br />Allison is the consummate friend who will support you, cheer you, and tell you when you're an idiot or fuck off when you've screwed up, but in the end they're there. I liked that there was a good give and take to their friendship and not everything had an easy solution. And let's face it, they have serious disagreements about Tim. <br /><br />Tim. We all had one of these at some point, the elusive, unreachable, ungettable get. Ben is goofy and awkward and squeezes his way into Tim's life--as barren as it is. Ben is the best thing that's ever happened to Tim and he can't accept it. Heart ripped out #1.<br /><br />Sucks, but first loves are like that. Reboot. What happens then is Ben's journey to find love. Real love. The kind that is proud, never hides, and surrounds you like a blanket--Jace. Talk about wonderful. Fucking love Jace so hard, and so does Ben. But, the past doesn't always stay in the past...<br /><br />Heart ripped out #2--bad choice<br /><br />Heart ripped out #3--I don't want to talk about it. Took me three days to even think about writing this review because of it. Maybe I'm a masochist, but I liked this story. I liked that there was a slightly non traditional trajectory with some realism. At the end, part of me felt like we got to eat our cake and have it, too. It's just a bittersweet cake. <br /><br />Overall, an emotional journey that slaps you around<br /><br />Favorite quote:<b>
  <blockquote>"‘ Teach me how to fly, my beautiful butterfly.’” He reached out and ruffled Ben’s hair, his version of a parting kiss."</blockquote>
</b></span>

<div id="review_883292832" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/883292832" />
    <a title=".Lili. " class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/8905618-lili"><img alt=".Lili. " src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1593508329p2/8905618.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">

  <span id="freeText4660251694421022499" style="display:none">Oh my god! Okay *exhale* <br />Full gamut of emotions. Haven't cried over a book in a while...now I need something funny to read...<br /><br />(A couple days later): After being unable to write more than the above for a review, being so overwhelmed, I've decided to make my reply my review :-)<br /><br />"I wasn't expecting anything like this. From the description, the cover and the beginning I thought that this was just going to be a light YA read. Not at all. It was really compelling in the that it examines idealism of the past and the the resultant impact upon one's present when one can't let go, ideas of alienation and self-acceptance, of dependence and self-love, of maturity, evolution, compatibility and why, of inexorable attraction and its effects, of fear and freedom, and seeming fate. It was such a powerful read for me hereby.<br /><br />The last third of the book has a swifter pace than that which precedes it and some reviews I've read said that people found it to be rushed....I can see how. But I find it to be strong all in all."<br /><br />I would definitely read work by this author again...after a suitable interval though, with some light stuff in between. Bell fulfills his intent illustrated in his bio really well. He communicates feelings of alienation and love that surrounds decisions deftly. This book deserves its accolades. <br /><br /><br /></span>

<div id="review_369510606" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/369510606" />
    <a title="Kaje Harper" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5309738-kaje-harper"><img alt="Kaje Harper" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1307630447p2/5309738.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/369510606?book_show_action=true">Jul 15, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kaje Harper" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kaje Harper" href="/user/show/5309738-kaje-harper">Kaje Harper</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer369510606" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17358287877446347733">This is a book about a first love that lingers. Ben's evolution as a gay man begins with a teenage crush on Tim, and like imprinting, Tim becomes fixed in Ben's core as the embodiment of the man he loves. Throughout their early days of hiding, of unequal partnering, rejection, and through all the years to follow, Tim remains somehow an essential part of Ben.<br/><br/>In the years they are apart, Ben meets a guy who is better for him in every way. Open, loving, out and responsible, Jace is a wonderful char</span>
  <span id="freeText17358287877446347733" style="display:none">This is a book about a first love that lingers. Ben's evolution as a gay man begins with a teenage crush on Tim, and like imprinting, Tim becomes fixed in Ben's core as the embodiment of the man he loves. Throughout their early days of hiding, of unequal partnering, rejection, and through all the years to follow, Tim remains somehow an essential part of Ben.<br /><br />In the years they are apart, Ben meets a guy who is better for him in every way. Open, loving, out and responsible, Jace is a wonderful character and worthy of Ben's love. So part of the stress in this novel, painful but true-to-life, is the way that Tim still dominates Ben's idea of love. By simply showing up, Tim can rock the solid relationship between Ben and Jace, and when he resorts to an all-out assault to get Tim back, he comes close to breaking it. How often have we seen this, though, where the loving partner cannot quite match the spark of the one who came before him? It hurts, but that doesn't mean it's not real. <br /><br />The ending of this book might have felt like a triumph of true love, if Tim were a more sympathetic character. I think it's mainly one episode in the middle, <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[when Tim has a friend pretend to be Jace's lover to break Ben and Jace up, <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> that forever lingers in my mind like a faint trace of smoke on the air, a reminder that this character, however much he has moved forward over the years, isn't as trustworthy as one would want for Ben. <br /><br />Well written and involving, with complex characters and interesting plot, this book is well worth a read as long as you don't go in expecting the sweet simple sense of resolution that a romance often brings.</span>
  <a data-text-id="17358287877446347733" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_551110738" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/551110738" />
    <a title="Natalie" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4856711-natalie"><img alt="Natalie" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1333768754p2/4856711.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/551110738?book_show_action=true">Mar 03, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Natalie" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Natalie" href="/user/show/4856711-natalie">Natalie</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4856711-natalie?shelf=coming-of-age">coming-of-age</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4856711-natalie?shelf=first-time">first-time</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4856711-natalie?shelf=friends-to-lovers">friends-to-lovers</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4856711-natalie?shelf=gfy-ofy">gfy-ofy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4856711-natalie?shelf=cover-love">cover-love</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4856711-natalie?shelf=broke-my-heart">broke-my-heart</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4856711-natalie?shelf=grief">grief</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4856711-natalie?shelf=borrowed">borrowed</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer551110738" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17032350619808881297">I really struggled with how to rate this. When I give a two-star rating, it's usually because the writing was mediocre or the plot bored me. Not so with this story. I was <i>into</i> it. I inhaled it in anxious gulps, desperate to get to the end. I read the spoilers beforehand. I knew what was going to happen. But I HATED how it unfolded. It was the author's job to make me love Tim, and he failed.<br/><br/>I'm going to start the second book right now, because apparently I'm a glutton for punishment, but mostly b</span>
  <span id="freeText17032350619808881297" style="display:none">I really struggled with how to rate this. When I give a two-star rating, it's usually because the writing was mediocre or the plot bored me. Not so with this story. I was <i>into</i> it. I inhaled it in anxious gulps, desperate to get to the end. I read the spoilers beforehand. I knew what was going to happen. But I HATED how it unfolded. It was the author's job to make me love Tim, and he failed.<br /><br />I'm going to start the second book right now, because apparently I'm a glutton for punishment, but mostly because I want to see if it changes my opinion of Tim.</span>
  <a data-text-id="17032350619808881297" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_904570600" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/904570600" />
    <a title="Thomas" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2018505-thomas"><img alt="Thomas" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1567953607p2/2018505.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/904570600?book_show_action=true">Apr 08, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Thomas" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Thomas" href="/user/show/2018505-thomas">Thomas</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781453875049" href="/book/show/10187586-something-like-summer">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2018505-thomas?shelf=read-on-kindle">read-on-kindle</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2018505-thomas?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2018505-thomas?shelf=own-electronic">own-electronic</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2018505-thomas?shelf=romance">romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2018505-thomas?shelf=lgbtq">lgbtq</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2018505-thomas?shelf=realistic-fiction">realistic-fiction</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer904570600" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7389394592275297460"><i>disappointment</i>: <b>noun</b> 1) the feeling of sadness or displeasure caused by the nonfulfillment of one's hopes or expectations. 2) the emotion experienced when you don't like a book that almost all of Goodreads appears to love: "Thomas's read of <i>Something Like Summer</i> was a disappointment"<br/><br/>So many things went wrong with this simple story of two high school boys who fall in love after an unfortunate collision. Ben Bentley, our protagonist, notices an attractive newcomer in his neighborhood right before </span>
  <span id="freeText7389394592275297460" style="display:none"><i>disappointment</i>: <b>noun</b> 1) the feeling of sadness or displeasure caused by the nonfulfillment of one's hopes or expectations. 2) the emotion experienced when you don't like a book that almost all of Goodreads appears to love: "Thomas's read of <i>Something Like Summer</i> was a disappointment"<br /><br />So many things went wrong with this simple story of two high school boys who fall in love after an unfortunate collision. Ben Bentley, our protagonist, notices an attractive newcomer in his neighborhood right before the school year starts. Tim Wyman, the object of Ben's affection, has a girlfriend: but that and much more changes when Ben and Tim's connection deepens and grows stronger.<br /><br />I still cannot comprehend the plot of this book. The story spans several decades, and yet I still feel as if nothing of real importance happened - Jay Bell jumps around from one event to another without developing the significance of any scene or storyline. At one point Ben trashes his high school journalism room because the editor of the newspaper removed the gay portion of his poem: Bell resolves that conflict in a couple of pages without Ben really learning anything at all. We never see Tim come to terms with his sexuality because whenever his character grows, Bell hides it behind a convenient time lapse or a "tell, don't show" moment. The entire second part of the book with Ben and Jace had no connection to any other section of the story, and it felt like Bell took the easy way out by including it.<br /><br />The secondary characters in this book saddened me because they fell so flat. Why does Allison, Ben's best friend, have a life that only revolves around Ben and struggles that are so easily solved whenever Ben shows up? Why is Jace perfect in every way possible? Near the end of the book, Ben thinks to himself that "there was so much more to Tim beneath the surface that others didn't see." Instead of telling us that, I wish Bell <i>showed</i> us Tim's depth instead of having him act like a scary stalker for a solid third of the book. Tim's behavior, while unrealistic and unexplained, also made me think about Bell's disconcerting portrayal of a healthy relationship - because Tim's obsession did cross into a creepy place several times.<br /><br />I wanted so much more from Ben. His entire character revolved around his romantic relationships with other guys. I wished to see his passions, his hobbies, and his personality expand as the book progressed. Instead, I felt that his perspective stayed the same throughout the entire novel, while only his relationships with those around him changed. If someone asked me to describe Ben's character, I would be unsure of what to say, because I can only think of bland generalities that could apply to almost anyone.<br /><br />Overall, <i>Something Like Summer</i> required little effort to read, but a lot of dedication to finish. It might make a good beach read for those who want a YA with decent writing and gay characters, though I would not recommend it due to its lack of substance. Still, I find myself in the minority with my opinion, and I am glad that others on Goodreads have enjoyed it.</span>
  <a data-text-id="7389394592275297460" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer1282595289398848464">Oh wow, and to think a craving for Kevin R. Free resulted in all that <i>angst</i>!<br/><br/>I can see why so many reviews are accompanied by spoiler tags (and thank goodness I didn't read <i>any</i> of them).   <span id="freeText1282595289398848464" style="display:none">Oh wow, and to think a craving for Kevin R. Free resulted in all that <i>angst</i>!<br /><br />I can see why so many reviews are accompanied by spoiler tags (and thank goodness I didn't read <i>any</i> of them). So read the blurb and avoid the reviews - just decide for yourself if you like this one.<br /><br />Personally, I really enjoyed this book, and the 5 stars I'm giving are well deserved, even if I spent a bunch of time yelling at Ben, "No! Don't do it!". I'm surprised by how many lengthy 1,2,&amp;3 star reviews I read where folks just didn't like the behaviour of the characters, or the way the plot went... regardless of whether or not we <i>like</i> a book, if it brings out such strong emotions in us maybe it deserves a higher rating. Well, just a thought.<br /><br />Anyway - really beautifully written &amp; I'm so glad I finally got around to listening to <i>Something Like Summer</i>. Kevin R. Free's performance is brilliant, he's a treasure and I truly wish he'd narrate more. As soon as I've recovered emotionally from this one, I'll look into more written by Jay Bell.</span>

<div id="review_1979898755" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1979898755" />
    <a title="Anja V" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/63418989-anja-v"><img alt="Anja V" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1506201959p2/63418989.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1979898755?book_show_action=true">Jun 01, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Anja V" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Anja V" href="/user/show/63418989-anja-v">Anja V</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781453875049" href="/book/show/10187586-something-like-summer">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/63418989-anja-v?shelf=lgbtqia">lgbtqia</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/63418989-anja-v?shelf=series-i-will-not-finish">series-i-will-not-finish</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/63418989-anja-v?shelf=overrated">overrated</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1979898755" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1359794635655708917"><b>I'm going to spoil the whole book, so don't continue reading if you mind. Also swearing.</b><br/><br/>HOLY FUCK, was that frustrating. You know, I thought I'd hit off Pride Month with a cute, heart-wrenching gay romance. <b>Well, think again. Instead of cute, I got creepy. Instead of heart-wrenching, I got head-banging on the table.</b> Almost every second page I just had to pause to cool down. At some point I actually thought it would get better now. HA HA HA no. It just got worse. <br/> <br/>I thought this would be a cute r</span>
  <span id="freeText1359794635655708917" style="display:none"><b>I'm going to spoil the whole book, so don't continue reading if you mind. Also swearing.</b><br /><br />HOLY FUCK, was that frustrating. You know, I thought I'd hit off Pride Month with a cute, heart-wrenching gay romance. <b>Well, think again. Instead of cute, I got creepy. Instead of heart-wrenching, I got head-banging on the table.</b> Almost every second page I just had to pause to cool down. At some point I actually thought it would get better now. HA HA HA no. It just got worse. <br /> <br />I thought this would be a cute romance. Instead Ben is fuCKING CREEPY, almost stalking Tim. He doesn't know ANYTHING about him, other than that he is hot , but still he walks past his house at least TWICE A DAY??? Also, Tim hangs out with the bullies from his school, so apparently he isn't the nicest guy, but still, when Ben accidentally causes him to sprain his ankle, he offers to nurse him for two weeks. He starts to skip school and neglect his family, to nurse a guy he doesn't know shit about, hoping it'll lead to sex, despite Tim repeatedly mentioning that he's straight. Let's be real, you only have to add the sentence "until one day his obsession takes a dark turn…" and you have a premise for a FUCKING PSYCHO THRILLER. <br />	<br />But of course Ben's dreams come true and the two of them actually start a relationship. Only problem, TIM HAS NO FUCKING PERSONALITY. Not only that Ben is a whining creep, but Tim is also uninteresting as fuck. Dear Jay Bell, how am I supposed to care about this relationship when I couldn't give less a shit about either the MC or the love interest? Honestly, we don't learn anything about Tim. Even know after finishing the book, the only thing unrelated to Ben that I know about Tim are that his parents are shitty af and that he paints. THAT'S IT. Throughout the book, Ben repeatedly is asked what he likes about Tim and his answer always is: 'There's more to him than his looks.' But he never really establishes what. <br />	<br />Also, FUCKING CHEATING. Tim is in a relationship when he and Ben start to hook up. I don't care that Tim doesn't care about her, that doesn't make it okay. He is in a relationship, that's all that matters. But we'll get back to cheating later, because foreshadowing, BEN IS A CHEATING SHIT.<br />	<br />Oh and this quote: <i>"Why are you even with her? You never have anything nice to say about her. She doesn't put out; she's not even the prettiest girl in school."</i> smh I have a lot of problems with this<br />	<br />also from reading US high school themed books and watching US high school themed movies one might believe that every single high school jock is an asshole - Idk about you but I have sporty friends and they're actually pretty nice<br />	<br />Now, remember that I already don't like neither Tim, nor Ben, not to mention their weird ass relationship. Then this happened: Ben wrote a gay-themed poem for his school paper, which gets published. Without his consent though, the teacher changes it into a heterosexual poem. Ben is understandably furious. His reaction though is <i>so stupid and unnecessary</i>. He goes to the journalism room to confront his teacher, but finds it empty. For some reason Tim shows up and then <b>encourages him to trash the whole room</b>, including the dark room. Like, why???? I get that he is angry, I really do, but why the fuck does he have to resort to violence? The other students of the journalism course seem to be the only ones that are nice to him in school and now he goes and fucking destroys all their creations?? That's such a dick move. And he doesn't even feel bad about it? In the end he admits to doing it, but only to save Tim's ass and he even says, he doesn't feel bad about it, because it feels like they made some sort of romantic memory together, Bonny and Clyde style, WTF??? <s>I'm already so done with these two assholes</s><br />	<br />Now let's skip forward. Tim's and Ben's relationship doesn't work out and Ben moves on. He meets Jace and the two of them start a relationship. Now, Jace is a freaking SAINT. I'm not saying this on a positive note. It's frustrating. Look, Ben and Jace are together for quite some time and they are COMMITTED. But someday Tim shows up and Ben starts meeting up with him. He knows he still has feelings for him, but tells himself nothing will happen. BUT HE FUCKING KNOWS HE HAS FEELINGS FOR HIM LIKE IT'S SO RUDE TO JACE. He eventually tells him and Jace is like, well sucks but it's fine and they even all go out together. ??????? what. Of course, Ben and Tim end up making out BECAUSE CHEATING IS SUCH A FUCKING COOL THING TO DO and Jace finds out and you know what he does? NOTHING he's like well first love and all, it's hard to get over that, but Idc WHAT. <br />	<br />Also remember how I said Ben was close to a stalker in the beginning? WELL APPARENTLY TIM LEARNED FROM HIM BECAUSE HE IS SO FUCKING CREEPY AND INNAPROPRIATE he just shows up to Jace and Ben's house, makes a lot of sexual jokes, even though Ben told him he is in a relationship and most of all HE MADE ONE OF HIS FELLOW STUDENTS TO GO TO THEIR HOUSE AND SLIP A NOTE THAT BASICALLY IS SUPPOSED TO BE PROVE THAT JACE IS CHEATING ON BEN ALL SO THAT THEY BREAK UP AND BEN GOES BACK TO TIM I'M NOT KIDDING AND YOU KNOW WHAT IT WORKS BEN AND JACE KIND OF BREAK UP AND BEN GOES BACK TO TIM well eventually Ben finds out that Tim was behind his note and I KID YOU NOT HE ENDS UP WITH JACE FUCKING AGAIN AND JACE IS JUST LIKE IDC I LOVE YOU LIKE HAVE A SPINE YOU IDIOT I hate all three of them at this point <br />	<br />And know, the most stupid thing is yet to happen<br />Ben and Jace are happy again, they even marry and them JACE FUCKING DIES <br />YES<br />HE JUST FUCKING DIES<br />AND THAT'S NOT EVEN IT <br />TWO YEARS LATER <br />BEN AND TIM <br />GET BACK TOGETHER <br />EVEN THOUGH <br />THEY HAVEN'T SEEN EACH OTHER FOR TWO FUCKING YEARS<br />JUST LIKE THAT <br /><s>I'm so done with this shit</s> I'm not even going to talk more detailed about the ending, it isn't worth my time <br />	<br />The only thing that sooths my anger is when I imagine how Tim and Ben, after having their big moment, suddenly realize that they have nothing in common anymore and it's just fucking awkward and they just sit next to each other in silence because honestly I get that you will always have a special place for you first love, but like no one can tell me that after TWO YEARS OF NO CONTACT you can just get back together without even checking first if you even still like each other it's so stupid</span>
  <a data-text-id="1359794635655708917" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

        <a title="Sara " class="user" itemprop="url" name="Sara " href="/user/show/5058304-sara">Sara </a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5058304-sara?shelf=boys-who-love-boys">boys-who-love-boys</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5058304-sara?shelf=kleenex-worthy">kleenex-worthy</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer685902635" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5226665614029083453">I know I say it often, "How do I review this book?" but honestly, how do I? I picked up Something like Summer (twice actually not realizing my blunder) because I was drawn to the bright orange of the cover with that bit of blue that caught my eye every time. One Sunday, when I was stuck in bed I wanted a book to bring my spirits up so I started this. What happened was me being sucked into a book that I did not stop reading until I was done. <br/><br/>Ben, what a strong character at such a young age. I wis</span>
  <span id="freeText5226665614029083453" style="display:none">I know I say it often, "How do I review this book?" but honestly, how do I? I picked up Something like Summer (twice actually not realizing my blunder) because I was drawn to the bright orange of the cover with that bit of blue that caught my eye every time. One Sunday, when I was stuck in bed I wanted a book to bring my spirits up so I started this. What happened was me being sucked into a book that I did not stop reading until I was done. <br /><br />Ben, what a strong character at such a young age. I wish that my children could have the sense of self that he does. I felt his "not stalkerish" crush on the new boy with the blue running shoes. I wanted him to be noticed, I wanted the new boy to SEE Ben and fall head over blue shoes for him instantly and I wanted this to be a story that would knock me on my butt. Did it ever!<br /><br />I love that this book spans a decade. There is beauty to a slow burn in romance that does it for me. Sure, insta love is also fantastic but this story wouldn't work that way. Ben and Tim, Tim and Ben. Good Lord. Let's just say I loved being in Ben's head and when he asks Tim to say something to him in Spanish I thought my heart would explode. I looked up the translation before Tim explains it and I melted. It was beyond beautiful and heart wrenching and stunning and, Le Sigh. <br /><br />There are at least a dozen or thirty moments that were like that for me. Tear my heart out why don't ya Jay Bell?!<br /><br />Now, I was not prepared for the road this story took but I love where it went. Seeing Ben grow and change and fight the instincts of a love sick teenager were gorgeous. Jay Bell certainly knows how to weave a story that sucks the reader and and it he did that with me. <br /><br />Let me just say that Tim was fantastic. I never once thought he was selfish, absent or mean when it came to Ben. When I found out that he was getting his own book I immediately went and one clicked that bad boy. I had to know what was going on in his head during this time. All this time. Ugh.<br /><br />Something Like Summer a roller coaster of a read with an intense climb into adoration followed by a swift down fall into love...for me that is. I just loved this story, so much. </span>
  <a data-text-id="5226665614029083453" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/642782893?book_show_action=true">Jun 16, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Marc | Rainbow Gold Reviews" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Marc | Rainbow Gold Reviews" href="/user/show/19769750-marc-rainbow-gold-reviews">Marc | Rainbow Gold Reviews</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/19769750-marc-rainbow-gold-reviews?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer642782893" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11184999973108768656">I loved this book ;) It reminded me of the YA series "Infernal Devices" in that it shows that there is not always only one person we could love, but that a lot depends on the right timing. A person can find happiness in different ways, but there is a right time and place for everything and every action has consequences. Life doesn't stop, it just continues around us and our choices shape the way our life continues, even if we would like it to go into another way. There are mistakes and regrets, </span>
  <span id="freeText11184999973108768656" style="display:none">I loved this book ;) It reminded me of the YA series "Infernal Devices" in that it shows that there is not always only one person we could love, but that a lot depends on the right timing. A person can find happiness in different ways, but there is a right time and place for everything and every action has consequences. Life doesn't stop, it just continues around us and our choices shape the way our life continues, even if we would like it to go into another way. There are mistakes and regrets, but if we spend all our energy trying to re-capture a moment that is already gone, refusing to move on, we might get stuck without energy to admire the beauty of what may still lie ahead of us. While it may be understandable to wish we could edit our mistakes, we have to accept even the moments in life we feel went wrong and follow where our actions lead us.<br /><br />There are so many different ways this novel could have played out with different timing, different decisions (for example whether or not to forgive indiscretions, whether or not to admit truth, whether to let fear or love rule us, whether to use our heads or little heads). It felt like a real story with very interesting characters as they navigate their lives :) I can recommend it without reservations :)</span>
  <a data-text-id="11184999973108768656" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
                  <em>
                    This review has been hidden because it contains spoilers. To view it,
                    <a href="#" onclick="Effect.toggle(&#39;reviewTextContainer286258171&#39;); return false;">click here.</a>
                  </em>
              <span id="reviewTextContainer286258171" class="readable"
                    style="display:none"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9060071348515035648">This easily could have been a 4/5 book. However, three things absolutely ruined it for me: 1) the sudden death of Jace, which seemed entirely too coincidental; it should have been foreshadowed at least a little bit; 2) Tim's douchebaggery increased exponentially as he got older; it was kind of understandable during the first part of the book (easily the best part), but convincing your ex that his current significant other cheated on him, just to get into his pants afterwards is NOT OKAY; and 3) </span>
  <span id="freeText9060071348515035648" style="display:none">This easily could have been a 4/5 book. However, three things absolutely ruined it for me: 1) the sudden death of Jace, which seemed entirely too coincidental; it should have been foreshadowed at least a little bit; 2) Tim's douchebaggery increased exponentially as he got older; it was kind of understandable during the first part of the book (easily the best part), but convincing your ex that his current significant other cheated on him, just to get into his pants afterwards is NOT OKAY; and 3) Ben, too, grew more and more unlikeable; at first, he was just a cute little nerd, but then he became more and more annoying as the story continued. The random subplots about Allison's father was incredibly out of nowhere, as if they were tacked on at the last minute to add even more drama. Due to all of that, I think it would've been a much better book if it had just ended at the end of the high school portion, after Ben and Tim broke up.</span>

<div id="review_1086226848" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1086226848" />
    <a title="wesley" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/36179338-wesley"><img alt="wesley" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1446832327p2/36179338.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1086226848?book_show_action=true">Oct 21, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="wesley" class="user" itemprop="url" name="wesley" href="/user/show/36179338-wesley">wesley</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/36179338-wesley?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1086226848" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer143789539804471577">This is the first M/M YA book that I’ve read and I cannot be grateful enough that I did read it because it has helped me come to terms with my sexuality. Being born in a country where both the state and the church have forged ideals of what should be the norm, being gay included, has forced people like me to hide deep in the closet. But after reading this early this year, the entire Something Like Series in fact, and hundreds of M/M books after that, I can at least say that I am now honest with </span>
  <span id="freeText143789539804471577" style="display:none">This is the first M/M YA book that I’ve read and I cannot be grateful enough that I did read it because it has helped me come to terms with my sexuality. Being born in a country where both the state and the church have forged ideals of what should be the norm, being gay included, has forced people like me to hide deep in the closet. But after reading this early this year, the entire Something Like Series in fact, and hundreds of M/M books after that, I can at least say that I am now honest with myself. I am gay and it will not change. <br /><br />It’s kind of funny how a series focused on ordinary lives of fictional people can have such a huge impact on your own. Somehow I can’t help but be envious of Ben for having to live an honest life despite the pain and sorrow that went along with it. I can’t help but wonder if there are real people out there like Ben and Tim who are living the life that they’ve wanted… no, needed. And that is what this series is all about to me. It’s HOPE. It’s hope that there’s someone out there perfect and waiting for me. It’s hope that although not everyone can be happy with who you are, at least the people that actually mattered support and love you all the way. It’s hope that despite the pain and hardships that are sure to come in trying to live a life of honestly, somehow it will all be worth it in the end. <br /><br />And although having to cling to this hope can be dangerous, I cannot let it go. Because having a window a little open to let the tiniest bit of air in is better than suffocating for keeping it closed. I aspire for a life like Ben’s because I know that a happy ending is possible. <br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="143789539804471577" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>
